[2024-02-19 16:03:47.416702] DEBUG: runsource: why is the sky blue?
[2024-02-19 16:04:04.935479] DEBUG: runsource: The sky appears blue to the human eye because of a phenomenon called Rayleigh scattering. When sunlight enters the Earth's atmosphere, it is made up of light of various colors—each of which has a different wavelength. Oxygen and nitrogen molecules in the Earth's atmosphere scatter the sunlight in all directions. 

Blue light is scattered more than other colors because it travels as shorter, smaller waves. This scattering causes the sky to look blue in the daytime. At sunrise and sunset, the sky can appear red or orange because the light is passing through more of the Earth's atmosphere, causing the blue light to scatter out of the line of sight and allowing the longer wavelengths of red and orange to dominate.
